Here's a summary of what I changed:\n\n## Summary\n\nThe `pointnet2_ops` extension was written for NVIDIA CUDA. PyTorch's `CUDAExtension` automatically hipifies `.cu`/`.cpp` sources and routes them through `hipcc` when running on a ROCm build of PyTorch, so the kernels themselves needed no changes. The fixes were all in the build config and Python wrappers:\n\n### `setup.py`\n- Removed the nvcc-only flags `-Xfatbin -compress-all` from `extra_compile_args[\"nvcc\"]` — these are rejected by `hipcc`/`clang++`.\n- Removed the `os.environ[\"TORCH_CUDA_ARCH_LIST\"] = \"3.7+PTX;...\"` assignment (invalid on ROCm; it would otherwise override the auto-detected `gfx*` arch flags from the PyTorch build). The original `known_feats.expand(*(known_feats.size()[0:2] + [unknown.size(1)]))` tries to concatenate a `torch.Size` (tuple) with a list, which crashes on modern Python. Changed to `known_feats.expand(known_feats.size(0), known_feats.size(1), unknown.size(1))` — same semantics, no math change.
